This was a large adult (probably female) Accipiter that was dull gray all over, with a black cap, and a matching dark face patch, unlike the face of a Cooper's Hawk. It looked like hybrid of a gray version of a Cooper's Hawk crossed with a Buteo e.g. Red-tailed Hawk. I vividly remember this bird, because it was my first adult Goshawk, having only seen immatures in the high mountains of Kern County, California, and Southeast Arizona eg. The Reef.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS328578798	2019-12-11 00:05:57	7846	species	Northern Goshawk	Accipiter gentilis			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Clark	US-NV-003	US-NV_943	33			Macks Canyon	L3746216	P	36.3506000	-115.6972000	2015-06-23	06:20:00	obsr368582	S24031981	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	250	4.828		2	1	G1328017	0	1	1			We were driving down the road with Pondersoa Pines all around us. A very large Northern Goshawk with a long tail with a zig-zag pattern of dark bands mixed with white exploded out of the clearing it was in. The bird crossed directly in front of us. Coloring of body of bird was brown. The breast appeared light colored. It had a much wider longer tail than the Sharp-shinned Hawk that was flying below the Northern Goshawk. One of the most stunning explosive flights I have ever seen of an Accipiter. A wonderful experience!!!

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS493106455	2019-08-21 19:33:05	7846	species	Northern Goshawk	Accipiter gentilis			1			Unknown Sex, Juvenile (1)	United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Douglas	US-NV-005		15			Lam Watah Nature Trail and Rabe Meadows	L3614376	H	38.9738559	-119.9409360	2017-04-29	11:00:00	obsr424260	S36464175	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	180	4.828		1	1		0	1	0			II saw this bird briefly, but got a good look at it as it glided past me.  What I saw was a large hawk, taking powerful wing beats before starting a glide and I thought buteo as I raised my binoculhars.  It did not present like the typical accipiter, the tail did not look wide and the wings were not straight.  The wings appeared bent and pointed, matching the silhouettes in Sibley's.  The underside was streaked, buffy and the streaking extended to flanks and underside.  The tail bands were not as large or regular as those of a Cooper's Hawk.  I must admit that I have never seen an immature Goshawk before although plenty of Cooper's Hawks.  I did not have time for a picture, it flew into the trees and I could not find it.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS260230127	2017-08-16 00:24:17	7846	species	Northern Goshawk	Accipiter gentilis			5				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Elko	US-NV-007	US-NV_971	9			Goshutes Hawkwatch	L808562	H	40.4253985	-114.2709489	1987-09-21	08:00:00	obsr45447	S18824024	Stationary	P21	EBIRD	540			4	0		0	1	0		In the fall of 1987, I was the official hawk counter on the Goshute Mtns Raptor Project. These are my data from the report I filed with the USFWS. This was a special day. Anticipating a Big Day, I had 3 assistants. Also, as was occasionally the case, we added an additional hour. The falcons, especially Peregrine Falcon were prone to pass later in the afternoon (as late as 6pm). The result was 17 species of raptor matching the then Big Day record published by the American Birding Association. Our total was subsequently published within the ABA record. To my knowledge, this stands as the greatest US tally for a stationary count.
